<span id="freeTextContainer9368696515476261221">From the bestselling author of <em>Along Came a Spider</em> and <em>Cat and Mouse</em>, a mesmerising tale of non-stop action and suspense.<br /><br />Nobody knows the underbelly of the city like New York cop John Stefanovitch. He's out to get Alexandre St-Germain, the most powerful member of the Midnight Club -- a secret international society of ruthless crime czars, all of whom are 'respectable' busi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9368696515476261221">From the bestselling author of <em>Along Came a Spider</em> and <em>Cat and Mouse</em>, a mesmerising tale of non-stop action and suspense.<br /><br />Nobody knows the underbelly of the city like New York cop John Stefanovitch. He's out to get Alexandre St-Germain, the most powerful member of the Midnight Club -- a secret international society of ruthless crime czars, all of whom are 'respectable' businessmen.<br /><br />And Stef's the ideal man for the job -- until he's levelled by a blast from St-Germain's shotgun and left for dead. Now, Stef is back, wheelchair-bound, yet sworn to destroy St-Germain.<br /><br />With the help of a beautiful journalist and a Harlem cop, Stef is determined to crack the Midnight Club. And he's up against odds that are as unknown as they are deadly!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_867459237">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/867459237" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2763719-john" class="left imgcol" title="John"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1386501977p2/2763719.jpg" alt="John" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/867459237?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2763719-john" class="user" title="John">John</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=james-patterson" class="actionLinkLite">james-patterson</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=mystery-detective-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-detective-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2763719-john?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer867459237">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7443307954401062181">An average Patterson thriller muddled by inconsistent writing and sappy melodrama. Certain aspects of this book I really liked, but there were some scenes I found incredibly stupid. Like when a dying policeman who knows the identity of his murderer decides to spend his last half-hour on Earth catching a taxi to his partner's apartment in order to tell him that he loves him--instead of, you know, passing on the crucial information to someone or maybe even getting himself to a hospital. Soon after</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7443307954401062181">An average Patterson thriller muddled by inconsistent writing and sappy melodrama. Certain aspects of this book I really liked, but there were some scenes I found incredibly stupid. Like when a dying policeman who knows the identity of his murderer decides to spend his last half-hour on Earth catching a taxi to his partner's apartment in order to tell him that he loves him--instead of, you know, passing on the crucial information to someone or maybe even getting himself to a hospital. Soon after writing this book, Patterson penned ALONG CAME A SPIDER and established himself as a publishing superstar. For better or worse, THE MIDNIGHT CLUB is basically a trial run for the Alex Cross series.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_318520329">

  <a href="/user/show/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum" class="left imgcol" title="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1369039029p2/4986986.jpg" alt="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/318520329?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 13, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4986986-tracey-allen-at-carpe-librum" class="user" title="Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum">Tracey Allen at Carpe Librum</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/828635.The_Midnight_Club" title="Paperback 9780007224890" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer318520329">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4069063407765586575">First published in 1989, I somehow missed reading The Midnight Club by James Patterson, not to be confused with his series the Women's Murder Club.<br /><br />The protagonist in The Midnight Club is John Stefanovitch, a New York cop confined to a wheelchair after being shot and left for dead by the Grave Dancer. Despite losing his wife to the Grave Dancer on the same chilling night, and undergoing years of rehabilitation, John is still on the force and as determined as ever to get his man.<br /><br />While John was fig</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4069063407765586575">First published in 1989, I somehow missed reading The Midnight Club by James Patterson, not to be confused with his series the Women's Murder Club.<br /><br />The protagonist in The Midnight Club is John Stefanovitch, a New York cop confined to a wheelchair after being shot and left for dead by the Grave Dancer. Despite losing his wife to the Grave Dancer on the same chilling night, and undergoing years of rehabilitation, John is still on the force and as determined as ever to get his man.<br /><br />While John was fighting and clawing back his life, the Grave Dancer was climbing the ladder of success, and is now part of an elite and secretive international unit of organised crime lords, otherwise known as the Midnight Club. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed having a male protagonist in a wheelchair who was attractive, strong, protective and driven without feeling sorry for himself or drinking himself into oblivion. Patterson steers clear of all the possible traps and cliches here, which makes The Midnight Club feel like a fresh piece of writing, despite it being 23 years old. <br /><br />There are references to the twin towers and a few other things that remind the reader of the passage of time however on the whole, this was an enjoyable crime novel with a very likeable good guy in New York cop John Stefanovitch and an equally well written bad guy.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4069063407765586575">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48281486">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9721427970254672315">I've been a long time fan of James Patterson and have read most everything he has written...with the exception of his earliest novels. So, I'm trying to go back and read Patterson's earlier books. <br />I have to say I was very disappointed in The Midnight Club. It just didn't live up to the quality I've grown accustomed too. Yes, I agree that some of the more recent Alex Cross books haven't been great but at least they kept my interest.<br />I finished The Midnight Club on Friday and am writing this on Mon</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9721427970254672315">I've been a long time fan of James Patterson and have read most everything he has written...with the exception of his earliest novels. So, I'm trying to go back and read Patterson's earlier books. <br />I have to say I was very disappointed in The Midnight Club. It just didn't live up to the quality I've grown accustomed too. Yes, I agree that some of the more recent Alex Cross books haven't been great but at least they kept my interest.<br />I finished The Midnight Club on Friday and am writing this on Monday. Honestly, I can't remember anything about the plot. At this point, I'm trying to decide if I am going to listen to this book again before it has to be returned to the library.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1012213784">

  <a href="/user/show/9797342-chris-french" class="left imgcol" title="Chris French"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1406856162p2/9797342.jpg" alt="Chris French" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1012213784?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 31, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9797342-chris-french" class="user" title="Chris French">Chris French</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9797342-chris-french?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1012213784">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7623436233218279969">Detective John Stefanovich is obsessed with bringing Alexander St. Germain, a.k.a. The Grave Dancer, to justice. There are several reasons for Stef’s obsession. He is a good cop and that’s what good cops do: they bring down the bad guys, but his vendetta against the Grave Dancer is way more personal than the average collar. St. Germain put him in a wheelchair then went to Stef’s house and killed his wife. Now Stef will use every weapon in his arsenal to bring The Grave Dancer down…but he doesn’t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7623436233218279969">Detective John Stefanovich is obsessed with bringing Alexander St. Germain, a.k.a. The Grave Dancer, to justice. There are several reasons for Stef’s obsession. He is a good cop and that’s what good cops do: they bring down the bad guys, but his vendetta against the Grave Dancer is way more personal than the average collar. St. Germain put him in a wheelchair then went to Stef’s house and killed his wife. Now Stef will use every weapon in his arsenal to bring The Grave Dancer down…but he doesn’t get the chance. Someone beats him to the punch and kills St. Germain themselves. This vigilante doesn’t stop with the Grave Dancer though. Top underworld figures start showing up dead all over the world. What’s going on and who is driving these killings are the questions Stef and ex news reporter now author Sarah McGinnis have to answer.<br /><br />I’ve never read the Alex Cross series, but I’ve heard a lot of people talk negatively about Patterson’s non-Alex Cross books. This one was great. The story line was awesome and believable with some twists you won’t see coming. St. Germain is a psychopath, literally, so his actions are so grotesque and unimaginable that your mind staggers when contemplating that there are actually people who could do these things. Stef and Sarah are both very likable characters and Patterson develops them well. There were several characters in the book so pay attention or you’ll have problems keeping them straight.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7623436233218279969">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6483847002797553141">Third James Patterson book I have ever read. Good solid police procedural about a policeman who develops a personal vendetta against an amoral kingpin mob boss and works with another police officer to try to bring him down as well as his cronies in the Midnight Club. I thought the first half was excellent (5 stars) but the second half was simply good (3 stars) so ended up with a three star rating. Quick reading suspenseful tale - worth the time.</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_906507360">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906507360" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11230128-anne" class="left imgcol" title="Anne"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Anne" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/906507360?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11230128-anne" class="user" title="Anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer906507360">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6629772821638060456"><br />I don't think James Patterson will ever write as good as he does when he writes about Alex Cross. However, this is the first NON Alex Cross book of Patterson's that I have been able to finish. The story in this book was a good one, but it got a little confusing with so many different members of the Club. I felt the author should have focused more on the one main villain in the Midnight Club rather than trying to draw in more of them and show their different personalities. This was a fairly decen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6629772821638060456"><br />I don't think James Patterson will ever write as good as he does when he writes about Alex Cross. However, this is the first NON Alex Cross book of Patterson's that I have been able to finish. The story in this book was a good one, but it got a little confusing with so many different members of the Club. I felt the author should have focused more on the one main villain in the Midnight Club rather than trying to draw in more of them and show their different personalities. This was a fairly decent read, but I felt that putting the lead character in a wheelchair was a forced flaw. Most of Patterson's lead characters are really not flawed at all, but this one was way too obvious. I felt that the love story was a bit predictable and it seemed forced to me. The contempt these two characters felt for each other at the beginning was a waste of time - it was obvious how that would turn out. All in all, not bad for not having Alex Cross. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6629772821638060456">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer482368434289359355">I've found that most of Patterson's early books just don't grab me, but this one was an exception. The writing style and quality was excellent, and foretold of the style and characters to come in his Alex Cross series. My primary complaint is that the main character dropped out of the book towards the end and, while I was glad the loose end was tied up in the epilogue, I missed his presence and found the bad guy's demise at the hands of me onto their rather disappointing. A good read, though, fe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText482368434289359355">I've found that most of Patterson's early books just don't grab me, but this one was an exception. The writing style and quality was excellent, and foretold of the style and characters to come in his Alex Cross series. My primary complaint is that the main character dropped out of the book towards the end and, while I was glad the loose end was tied up in the epilogue, I missed his presence and found the bad guy's demise at the hands of me onto their rather disappointing. A good read, though, feeling much more like the author's recent writings rather that older. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/251220275?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5860033-lynn" class="user" title="Lynn">Lynn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer251220275">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9183416837494879733">There is nothing not to like about a book written by James Patterson, although this one lacked some of the fluidity of his other books, That's probably because it was written in the early 1980's, early days in Patterson's writing career.<br /><br />The book centers around the "Midnight Club" or just "Club", a new breed of international organized crime bosses who have one foot in respectable business pursuits and the other in the underworld. They always seem to elude the police, but a group of NYPD officers,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9183416837494879733">There is nothing not to like about a book written by James Patterson, although this one lacked some of the fluidity of his other books, That's probably because it was written in the early 1980's, early days in Patterson's writing career.<br /><br />The book centers around the "Midnight Club" or just "Club", a new breed of international organized crime bosses who have one foot in respectable business pursuits and the other in the underworld. They always seem to elude the police, but a group of NYPD officers, and later, just two, set out to stop them in unorthodox ways. The central of these characters is John Stevanovich, a homicide detective who has been pursuing one mobster in particular for many years, and bears the scars to prove it. <br /><br />Also involved is Sarah McGinnis, a former reporter turned author, whose path crosses that of Stevanovich, and in true James Patterson fashion, an alliance and love story emerges to offset the non-stop blood and guts surrounding the mob.<br /><br />Definitely worth a read for the true James Patterson fan. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9183416837494879733">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_20654633">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20654633" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/985335-gina" class="left imgcol" title="Gina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1367005744p2/985335.jpg" alt="Gina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/20654633?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 21, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/985335-gina" class="user" title="Gina">Gina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer20654633">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16299283122218250507">It's 1:51 am and I just finished The Midnight Club. I'm yawning, but it was such an awesome novel, I had to write my review right away, LOL!<br /><br />I thought the characters were all strong individuals. After what Stef (NYPD Detective John Stefanovich) had gone through and endured, his raw determination from the beginning to the ending of this novel is nothing short of awe-inspiring and speechlessly astounding. I don't believe I've ever read a character as brave without meaning to be as Stef was. He trul</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16299283122218250507">It's 1:51 am and I just finished The Midnight Club. I'm yawning, but it was such an awesome novel, I had to write my review right away, LOL!<br /><br />I thought the characters were all strong individuals. After what Stef (NYPD Detective John Stefanovich) had gone through and endured, his raw determination from the beginning to the ending of this novel is nothing short of awe-inspiring and speechlessly astounding. I don't believe I've ever read a character as brave without meaning to be as Stef was. He truly is a joy, and it really is too bad that Patterson didn't write more novels starring Stef. He is a character I'll never forget.<br /><br />Sarah is a strong woman, even when facing the hardest situations. She does what she has to do and damn the concequences. I just wish she'd been able to give her ex-husband a real piece of her mind. I know I would like to.<br /><br />Isiah Parker isn't completely original, but the things he does and how he goes about doing them are almost shocking. The ending, though not a complete surprise, has you cheering! Vigilante-style or not, it still has you cheering.<br /><br />Alexandre St. Germain... the French bad guy. A man you immediately hate, loathe, despise and abominate, and you can actually feel the fear he instills in the characters.<br /><br />The plot wasn't the most creative - mob-style with the usual tactics - I thought it could have used a little more in the originality department. The twist in the novel, I actually saw coming, knowing what had happened at the beginning of the novel and if you remember the 'street law' as you go through the book, it's almost certainly expected. But I think I had more interest in the characters than in the goings-on. <br /><br />Some say it isn't Patterson's best novel. Although I really hate to agree with that, I actually have to. But the point is to also remember that he wrote this before he even started his Alex Cross series. I think for some, they'll be expecting something like his Cross series, and I know some will feel let-down in some way. So, for some strange reason, I feel the need to point out that this novel had first been published back in 1989. Had I read it back then, I'm sure it would have rated an excellent and excited 5 stars. Having read the kind of suspense and thriller novels that are published today, sure, this one is kind of lacking in luster. However, I bet you it was excellent in 1989.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16299283122218250507">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_96965274">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96965274" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3534502-julie" class="left imgcol" title="Julie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448942642p2/3534502.jpg" alt="Julie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/96965274?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 15, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3534502-julie" class="user" title="Julie">Julie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2090050.The_Midnight_Club" title="Paperback 9780446676410" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3534502-julie?shelf=thriller-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3534502-julie?shelf=crime-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3534502-julie?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer96965274">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6286358507905367009">I finally finished this Patterson book. While it was good, it wasn't one of my favorites. This is one of his earlier novels (published in 1989) and it has a somewhat different style than his more recent stories. The chapter length was still very short, making it a quick read. And there was an element of romance between two of the main characters like most of his current reads. The excitement that was building at the end of the book was also very good. I found myself skipping ahead a page or two</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6286358507905367009">I finally finished this Patterson book. While it was good, it wasn't one of my favorites. This is one of his earlier novels (published in 1989) and it has a somewhat different style than his more recent stories. The chapter length was still very short, making it a quick read. And there was an element of romance between two of the main characters like most of his current reads. The excitement that was building at the end of the book was also very good. I found myself skipping ahead a page or two towards the end just to see what would happen and then going back and reading the chapter in its entirety. I kind of felt like I would be cheating if I didn't read it thoroughly (kind of goofy, but just one of my many quirks)! Anyway, the big difference I noticed was that this didn't have the cliffhangers at the end of the chapters like his more recent books do. I really enjoy Patterson and one of the reasons is the thrilling pace of the story and the exciting end of each chapter. Without that, it made it easy to set this book aside and find something else to occupy my time. Normally I have a hard time stopping once I begin one of his books. With this one, it wasn't that difficult. This was still a good book, just not one of his better ones.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6286358507905367009">...more</a>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/10767506-courtney" class="user" title="Courtney">Courtney</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer363845654">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13284496237451335514">I'm going to start by saying it took me about a month maybe a bit longer to get through this one. It wasn't longer, about the same length. It just took me way too long. <br />The novel is about Organized crime and the NYPD trying to fight it. What they don't realize is how they are always one step behind the top mob bosses and business men involved in these mob and drug wars. <br />The main character is John Stefanovich. He meets a writer Sarah McGinnis, and they start talking about the "Midnight Club" and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13284496237451335514">I'm going to start by saying it took me about a month maybe a bit longer to get through this one. It wasn't longer, about the same length. It just took me way too long. <br />The novel is about Organized crime and the NYPD trying to fight it. What they don't realize is how they are always one step behind the top mob bosses and business men involved in these mob and drug wars. <br />The main character is John Stefanovich. He meets a writer Sarah McGinnis, and they start talking about the "Midnight Club" and how to go about catching and prosecuting them. <br />Through all of this, they form a close bond and eventually a relationship. <br />Stefanovich is confined to a wheel chair after being shot. He lost his wife and his partner of many years. <br />It takes you through some of his struggles of being a cop. <br /><br /><br />One thing I noticed while reading through this one is, I didn't really care about any of the characters. <br />Thats a risk writers have to take with stand-alone novels. Most of Patterson's books come in series so it is easier to get attached to the characters. <br />But with this one, I had no connection which ultimately made it more difficult to get through. <br /><br /><br />Overall <br />3/5 <br />The ending of the novel picked up and kept me engaged, but the road there was bumpy!</span>

      <a href="/user/show/1196851-aaron" class="user" title="Aaron">Aaron</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer47904222">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5791350168635949140">This is another of James Patterson's older titles. I am digging through the old ones since everyone says they are better than the new ones that have been coming out. Generally I like them.<br /><br />The main character for this one is a cop named John Stefanovich. He is a different kind of hero since he is confronted with living life in a wheelchair. He has looked into the possibility of corrective surgery, but it seems like doctors are indicated that there is a greater chance of causing more harm, leading</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5791350168635949140">This is another of James Patterson's older titles. I am digging through the old ones since everyone says they are better than the new ones that have been coming out. Generally I like them.<br /><br />The main character for this one is a cop named John Stefanovich. He is a different kind of hero since he is confronted with living life in a wheelchair. He has looked into the possibility of corrective surgery, but it seems like doctors are indicated that there is a greater chance of causing more harm, leading to his being a quadriplegic.<br /><br />In his current case, Stefanovich is on the hunt of Alexandre St. Germain, a "wet" worker (or assassin) that has close ties to a secret society called the Midnight Club. The membership is made up of high ranking criminals from all across the world. They like to parade themselves as being honest and respectable, but they are really ruthless people willing to do what ever it takes to get money and power.<br /><br />What makes the investigation so interesting is that Stefanovich owes his handicap to St. Germain. He actually lost the use of his legs when he was shot by St. Germain. Their history is even deeper as the French-born criminal is also responsible for the death of Stefanovich's wife.<br /><br />Stefanovich finds help in his search from Sarah McGinniss, a bestselling author of true crime. They quickly learn that they make a good investigative team ... as well as being romantic partners.<br /><br />The book definitely has all the elements that have made Patterson such a popular author. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5791350168635949140">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer444206362">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16378138941400685757">This novel was a classic James Patterson "keep you on your toes and guessing" kind of book. I love the crime/suspense/thriller genre more than any other and this book definitely satisfied that hunger for great suspenseful literature. "The Midnight Club" not only gives you a taste of gritty-street crime but also the behind the scenes life of New York detective John Stevonovich. <br /><br />Throughout the entire book you learn more about John's feelings and how he goes through everyday life with the images an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16378138941400685757">This novel was a classic James Patterson "keep you on your toes and guessing" kind of book. I love the crime/suspense/thriller genre more than any other and this book definitely satisfied that hunger for great suspenseful literature. "The Midnight Club" not only gives you a taste of gritty-street crime but also the behind the scenes life of New York detective John Stevonovich. <br /><br />Throughout the entire book you learn more about John's feelings and how he goes through everyday life with the images and thoughts of revenge in the back of his mind. The shocking parts in the book for me were <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[ the loss of his wife, his best friend, and the man who took everything from him being brought to justice<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[. But those all took time to unfold and piecing together the parts was even more intriguing. <br /><br />There are 40 some chapters all set up so that each chapter is from a different characters view and their situation. Each chapter starts off where that person is and and the date. This adds perspective to the book and offers a different look than just the main characters view the entire time. While reading the book in this form I got to understand attach to the different characters and their feelings. <br /><br />Now I love a good story but what I need in a book is some solid action and gritty gunfights that break out when you least expect it. Every detail from bullets leaving the chamber of a magnum handgun to the impact on the target it hits to everything in between. This novel had all of that and forced me to keep reading. I found this book to be changing and flat out emotionally moving. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16378138941400685757">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7035052611191415402">Started last night as a break from 16th century England. One more to go there before I leave for good(until Hilary Mantel's last Cromwell book comes out that is). I picked this one up from where it was lying around... at work in the break room I think. Never read this author before and I'm not really impressed so far. You know you're in hack-land when the "steaming mugs" of coffee come out. So far the plot, action and mystery are compelling enough. Very violent and derivative of course. Good wit</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7035052611191415402">Started last night as a break from 16th century England. One more to go there before I leave for good(until Hilary Mantel's last Cromwell book comes out that is). I picked this one up from where it was lying around... at work in the break room I think. Never read this author before and I'm not really impressed so far. You know you're in hack-land when the "steaming mugs" of coffee come out. So far the plot, action and mystery are compelling enough. Very violent and derivative of course. Good with the New York landmarks. That always helps.<br /><br />More "progress" last night. This all seems very formulaic. Reminds me of Joseph Wambaugh in fact only on the East Coast. Big body count so far plus episodes of rank cruelty and depravity. Still... competently written I suppose. I'm just looking for the endgame now. The twist that comes halfway through was entirely predictable. I doubt I'll be reading this author again.<br /><br />Finally wrapped up this quick and only semi-entertaining read. Mr. Patterson's a hack but no worse than many others: Wambaugh, Parker, Hillerman, Kellerman, Connelley etc. At times I was annoyed with the whole romance crap between Sarh and Stef... Blecch! and then there's the obligatory sequence of the protagonists being incredibly stupid in order for them(or others) to be put into peril. The endgame was handled well enough but I can do without the moralizing. And by the way, it's Ft. Sill not Ft. Sills. 2.75 rounds up to a weak 3*.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7834894297749130844">I rarely give five stars to a book I've read, this was an exceptional mystery that kept me reading as fast as my eyes could move; with my heart pounding just as hard. This is an earlier mystery by James Patterson and had me on the edge of my seat. Even though I anticipated "something" was about to happen (and sometimes anticipated the right something), when it happened, it was still unexpected in the manner it occurred - no Hollywood cliche's here. The book centers on a police detective left dis</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7834894297749130844">I rarely give five stars to a book I've read, this was an exceptional mystery that kept me reading as fast as my eyes could move; with my heart pounding just as hard. This is an earlier mystery by James Patterson and had me on the edge of my seat. Even though I anticipated "something" was about to happen (and sometimes anticipated the right something), when it happened, it was still unexpected in the manner it occurred - no Hollywood cliche's here. The book centers on a police detective left disabled by a criminal's bullet, his eventual ability to be part of the investigative team hunting the criminal down (not just any criminal, but someone involved in drugs, prostitution, murder and torture). The detective, Stefanovich, teams up with a journalist who has been researching this particular criminal and becomes quite involved in not only the on-going criminal investigation, but with the story behind the story. Torture (no gory details), kidnapping, shootings, massacres (no gory details) and betrayal by someone within the brotherhood. Elements needed for a good crime story, and this one had them all.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7834894297749130844">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/16240899-jody" class="left imgcol" title="Jody"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1406668199p2/16240899.jpg" alt="Jody" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/985636740?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16240899-jody" class="user" title="Jody">Jody</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer985636740">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3409511802088435035">This was a "filler" book for me, something you read because you must read, but something that's just filling the gaps while you wait for the next big novel to hit you. It took me a while to get into it, and then just as I was, it suddenly ended. Usually I like Pattersons quick, no frills approach to writing, but it didn't work so well this time for me.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1453671535?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 15, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/49473665-besanth" class="user" title="Besanth">Besanth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1453671535">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11979294406557842234">The first half of this book, I thought I was drowning in boredom of a monotonous written novel. However, throughout the second half of the book, I was greeted with a somewhat mild plot twist.<br /><br />Although I had a pretty pessimistic idea of this book throughout reading it, once I was done, I can conclude that it was a great read.<br /><br />If you're into more flat out constant writes that doesn't take you through a never-ending roller coaster ride of emotions, then this book would suit you just fine.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16607856886185260518">I have liked almost all of the James Patterson books I have read. This one was about organized crime and the upstanding citizens who fall into it. I did think the ending with the Midnight Club could have been better. Through the whole book they (the authorities) could get nowhere with these guys then, all of a sudden, in L.A...............well, I don't want to give it away. But the book is exciting from beginning to end.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16931549968779990989">This was a very interesting mystery with suspense and intrigue. There was a lot of action--a fast-paced drama. I liked the police detective and the reporter/novelist characters. This seemed different from many of the James Patterson books I have read. I liked the short chapters and found this book a quick read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SRHrVGP5XsGK/uF0D2k0El5ItGxfUw3szQJ+ETb8/HEsxdSHkStKOwYmlc9xCNKgF793dRaOSkanC3uD+mkKNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0yW6eD40NZvDa5H3yktk7oSdOEeBKsVGbXH0WM7aun+28YWrzOYhYU+z5Uy0KoJczWr7Xsj3guwHePHKAk9MOg==')})
  }

Patterson writes like the love child of Henry Miller and Mary Karr, with all the contradictions that implies -- a philosopher who thinks best over a glass of fine wine; an ex-Catholic still haunted by the image of the Crucifixion; an irreverent political satirist whose patriotism flies the flag of another iconoclast, Thomas Paine. Patterson grew up with a foot planted in each of two worlds -- one in Washington DC, the Capital of the Empire as he calls it, where the wheels of power spin, and one in rural Ontario, where his Canadian mother insisted the family spend their summers. His father, one of the wizards of twentieth century newspaper publishing, introduced him to the city\'s wheels of money and power, which he would later navigate as an entrepreneur, starting his first business at 20. But those Canadian summers introduced him to a different world - one where a cedar strip boat was better than any car, and where the ghosts of those who\'d previously inhabited the family\'s island house floated out over the water of Lovesick Lake.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson">About James Patterson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3780.James_Patterson"><img alt="3780" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1284492096p2/3780.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14556034059467152081"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patter</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14556034059467152081"><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.com">Offical US Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespatterson.co.uk">Offical UK Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.jamespattersonya.com">Offical James Patterson Young Adult Site</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.middleschoolbook.com">Offical Site for James Patterson's Middle School Series</a><br /><br /><br /><br />The subject of a <em>Time</em> magazine feature called, "The Man Who Can't Miss," James Patterson is the bestselling author of the past year, bar none, with more than 16 million books sold in North America alone. In 2007, one of every fifteen hardcover fiction books sold was a Patterson title. In the past three years, James has sold more books than any other author (according to Bookscan), and in total, James's books have sold an estimated 220 million copies worldwide. He is the first author to have #1 new titles simultaneously on <em>The New York Times</em> adult and children's lists and is the only author to have five new hardcover novels debut at #1 on the list in one year—a record-breaking feat he's accomplished every year since 2005. To date, James Patterson has had nineteen consecutive #1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling novels, and holds the <em>New York Times</em> record for most Hardcover Fiction bestselling titles by a single author (63 total), which is also a Guinness World Record.<br /><br /><br /><br />From his James Patterson Pageturner Awards (which rewarded groups and individuals for creative and effective ways to spread the joy of reading) to his website <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.readkiddoread.com">ReadKiddoRead.com</a> (which helps adults find books that kids are sure to love) to his regular donations of thousands of books to troops overseas, Patterson is a lifelong champion of books and reading. His first foray into books for all ages was the critically acclaimed Maximum Ride series, which debuted on the New York Times bestsellers list at #1 and remained there for twelve straight weeks. The series has so far made appearances on <em>The New York Times</em> bestsellers lists ninety-four cumulative times, proving that kids of all ages love page turners. He captured the attention of boy readers with the Daniel X series, and his third series for readers of all ages debuted in December 2009 with <em>Witch &amp; Wizard</em>, which spent five consecutive weeks atop the <em>New York Times</em> bestsellers list.<br /><br /><br /><br />Patterson is the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past dozen years, featuring Alex Cross and including the Hollywood-adapted "Along Came a Spider" and "Kiss the Girls," starring Academy Award-winning actor Morgan Freeman. He is also the creator of the #1 new detective series of the past five years, featuring Lindsay Boxer and the other members of the Women's Murder Club, from which the ABC television drama series was adapted. He has authored books behind six films on the Hollywood fast-track, including the upcoming Maximum Ride movie forthcoming from Avi Arad, the producer of X-Men and Spiderman.<br /><br /><br /><br />He is the author of novels—from The Thomas Berryman Number (1976) to Honeymoon (2005)—that have won awards including the Edgar, the BCA Mystery Guild's Thriller of the Year, the International Thriller of the Year award, and the Reader's Digest Reader's Choice Award. And, he has won a Children's Choice Book Council's Children's Choice Awards "Author of the Year" award (2010).<br /><br /><br /><br />One of Forbes magazine's Celebrity 100, James made a guest appearance on the popular FOX TV show "The Simpsons" in March, 2007.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14556034059467152081">...more</a>

    </div>
